href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>170 billion</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.stockholm.se/">www<wbr />.stockholm<wbr />.se</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Stockholm</b> <sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>. It has the most populous urban area in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> as well as in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>. 1 million people live in the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Municipality" title="Stockholm Municipality">municipality</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SCB2014_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCB2014-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> approximately 1.6&#160;million in the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_urban_area" title="Stockholm urban area">urban area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-StockholmUrbanArea_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StockholmUrbanArea-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and 2.4&#160;million in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Stockholm" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Stockholm">metropolitan area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SCB2014_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCB2014-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The city stretches across fourteen islands where <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4laren" title="M\xc3\xa4laren">Lake M\xc3\xa4laren</a> flows into the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>. Outside the city to the east, and along the coast, is the island chain of the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm archipelago">Stockholm archipelago</a>. The area has been settled since the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/6th_millennium_BC" title="6th millennium BC">6th millennium BC</a>, and was founded as a city in 1252 by Swedish statesman <a href="/wiki/Birger_Jarl" title="Birger Jarl">Birger Jarl</a>. It is also the county seat of <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_County" title="Stockholm County">Stockholm County</a>.\n</p><p>Stockholm is the cultural, media, political, and economic centre of Sweden. The Stockholm region alone accounts for over a third of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and is among the top 10 regions in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> by <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">GDP per capita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Ranked as an alpha-<a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> it is the largest in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> and the main centre for <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">corporate headquarters</a> in the Nordic region.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The city is home to some of Europe\'s top ranking universities, such as the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_School_of_Economics" title="Stockholm School of Economics">Stockholm School of Economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karolinska_Institutet" class="mw-redirect" title="Karolinska Institutet">Karolinska Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/KTH_Royal_Institute_of_Technology" title="KTH Royal Institute of Technology">KTH Royal Institute of Technology</a> and Stockholm University.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> ceremonies and banquet at the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Concert_Hall" title="Stockholm Concert Hall">Stockholm Concert Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a>. One of the city\'s most prized museums, the <a href="/wiki/Vasa_Museum" title="Vasa Museum">Vasa Museum</a>, is the most visited non-art museum in Scandinavia.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_metro" title="Stockholm metro">Stockholm metro</a>, opened in 1950, is well known for the decor of its stations; it has been called the longest art gallery in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/Friends_Arena" title="Friends Arena">national football arena</a> is located north of the city centre, in <a href="/wiki/Solna_Municipality" title="Solna Municipality">Solna</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_Globe" title="Ericsson Globe">Ericsson Globe</a>, the national indoor arena, is in the southern part of the city. The city was the host of the <a href="/wiki/1912_Summer_Olympics" title="1912 Summer Olympics">1912 Summer Olympics</a>, and hosted the equestrian portion of the <a href="/wiki/1956_Summer_Olympics" title="1956 Summer Olympics">1956 Summer Olympics</a> otherwise held in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne, Victoria</a>, Australia.\n</p><p>Stockholm is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sweden" title="Government of Sweden">Swedish government</a> and most of <a href="/wiki/Government_agencies_in_Sweden" title="Government agencies in Sweden">its agencies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> including the highest courts in the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Sweden" title="Judiciary of Sweden">judiciary</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residencies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Sweden" title="Monarchy of Sweden">Swedish monarch</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Sweden" title="Prime Minister of Sweden">Prime Minister</a>. The government has its seat in the <a href="/wiki/Rosenbad" title="Rosenbad">Rosenbad</a> building, the <a href="/wiki/Riksdag" title="Riksdag">Riksdag</a> (Swedish parliament) is seated in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Stockholm" title="Parliament House, Stockholm">Parliament House</a>, and the Prime Minister\'s residence is adjacent at <a href="/wiki/Sager_House" title="Sager House">Sager House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Palace" title="Stockholm Palace">Stockholm Palace</a> is the official residence and principal workplace of the Swedish monarch, while <a href="/wiki/Drottningholm_Palace" title="Drottningholm Palace">Drottningholm Palace</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> on the outskirts of Stockholm, serves as the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Royal Family">Royal Family</a>\'s private residence.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Drottningholm_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drottningholm-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" model</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Air_quality"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Air quality</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Public_Transportation"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public Transportation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-32"><a href="#The_City_Line_Project"><span class="tocnumber">9.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">The City Line Project</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Roads"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Roads</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-34"><a href="#Congestion_charges"><span class="tocnumber">9.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Congestion charges</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Ferries"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Ferries</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#City_bikes"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">City bikes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Airports"><span class="tocnumber">9.5</span> <span class="toctext">Airports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Inter-city_trains"><span class="tocnumber">9.6</span> <span class="toctext">Inter-city trains</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#International_rankings"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">International rankings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#Twin_cities_and_towns"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Twin cities and towns</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Stockholm" title="History of Stockholm">History of Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Suecia_1-013_;_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg/180px-Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg/270px-Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg/360px-Suecia_1-013_%3B_Stockholm_fr%C3%A5n_%C3%B6ster-right_side_detail.jpg class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail of engraving of Stockholm from <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text"><a href="/wiki/Suecia_Antiqua_et_Hodierna" title="Suecia Antiqua et Hodierna">Suecia Antiqua et Hodierna</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Erik_Dahlbergh" title="Erik Dahlbergh">Erik Dahlbergh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willem_Swidde" title="Willem Swidde">Willem Swidde</a>, printed in 1693.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg/180px-Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg/270px-Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg/360px-Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1895" data-file-height="1274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_panorama_1868.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama over Stockholm around 1868 as seen from a <a href="/wiki/Hot_air_balloon" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot air balloon">hot air balloon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen,_Stockholm_(5246272896).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg/220px-Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg/330px-Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg/440px-Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen%2C_Stockholm_%285246272896%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="819" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamngatan_and_Strandv%C3%A4gen,_Stockholm_(5246272896).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stockholm in 1917</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg/180px-Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg/270px-Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg/360px-Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5544" data-file-height="3701" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gamla_stan_February_2013_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Old Town of Stockholm (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Gamla stan</a></i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Ice Age, around 8,000 BC, there were already many people living in what is today the Stockholm area, but as temperatures dropped, inhabitants moved south. Thousands of years later, as the ground thawed, the climate became tolerable and the lands became fertile, people began to migrate back to the North. At the intersection of the Baltic Sea and lake <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4laren" title="M\xc3\xa4laren">M\xc3\xa4laren</a> is an archipelago site where the <a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Old Town</a> of Stockholm was first built from about 1000 CE by Vikings. They had a positive trade impact on the area because of the trade routes they created.\n</p><p>Stockholm\'s location appears in <a href="/wiki/Saga" title="Saga">Norse sagas</a> as <a href="/wiki/Agnafit" title="Agnafit">Agnafit</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Heimskringla" title="Heimskringla">Heimskringla</a> in connection with the legendary king <a href="/wiki/Agne" title="Agne">Agne</a>. The earliest written mention of the name Stockholm dates from 1252, by which time the mines in <a href="/wiki/Bergslagen" title="Bergslagen">Bergslagen</a> made it an important site in the iron trade. The first part of the name (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish-language text">stock</i>) means log in Swedish, although it may also be connected to an old German word (<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Stock</i>) meaning <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortification</a>. The second part of the name (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish-language text">holm</i>) means islet and is thought to refer to the islet <a href="/wiki/Helgeandsholmen" title="Helgeandsholmen">Helgeandsholmen</a> in central Stockholm. According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Eric_Chronicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Chronicles">Eric Chronicles</a></i> the city is said to have been founded by <a href="/wiki/Birger_Jarl" title="Birger Jarl">Birger Jarl</a> to protect Sweden from sea invasions made by <a href="/wiki/Karelia_(historical_province_of_Finland)" title="Karelia (historical province of Finland)">Karelians</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Sigtuna" title="Sigtuna">pillage of Sigtuna</a> on Lake M\xc3\xa4laren in the summer of 1187.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stockholm\'s core, the present Old Town (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Gamla Stan</a></i>) was built on the central island next to Helgeandsholmen from the mid-13th century onward. The city originally rose to prominence as a result of the Baltic trade of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. Stockholm developed strong economic and cultural linkages with <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="L\xc3\xbcbeck">L\xc3\xbcbeck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gda\xc5\x84sk">Gda\xc5\x84sk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visby" title="Visby">Visby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Reval</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a> during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Between 1296 and 1478 Stockholm\'s City Council was made up of 24 members, half of whom were selected from the town\'s German-speaking burghers.\n</p><p>The strategic and economic importance of the city made Stockholm an important factor in relations between the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Danish_monarchs" title="List of Danish monarchs">Danish Kings</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a> and the national independence movement in the 15th century. The Danish King <a href="/wiki/Christian_II_of_Denmark" title="Christian II of Denmark">Christian II</a> was able to enter the city in 1520. On 8 November 1520, a massacre of opposition figures called the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Bloodbath" title="Stockholm Bloodbath">Stockholm Bloodbath</a> took place and set off further uprisings that eventually led to the breakup of the Kalmar Union. With the accession of <a href="/wiki/Gustav_I_of_Sweden" title="Gustav I of Sweden">Gustav Vasa</a> in 1523 and the establishment of royal power, the population of Stockholm began to grow, reaching 10,000 by 1600.\n</p><p>The 17th century saw Sweden grow into a major European power, reflected in the development of the city of Stockholm. From 1610 to 1680 the population multiplied sixfold. In 1634, Stockholm became the official capital of the Swedish empire. Trading rules were also created that gave Stockholm an essential monopoly over trade between foreign merchants and other Swedish and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a> territories.  In 1697, <a href="/wiki/Tre_Kronor_(castle)" title="Tre Kronor (castle)">Tre Kronor (castle)</a> burned and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Palace" title="Stockholm Palace">Stockholm Palace</a>.\n</p><p>Throughout Sweden\'s history, <a href="/wiki/Walls_of_Stockholm" title="Walls of Stockholm">walls</a> were created in Stockholm to defend the city from attacks. These defensive walls were modified throughout the 13th to the 16th century. In 1625, a large fire occurred called the <a href="/wiki/Great_Stockholm_Fire_of_1625" title="Great Stockholm Fire of 1625">"Stora V\xc3\xa5delden"</a>; English translation meaning "Large Wildfire." This fire destroyed the southwestern section of Stadsholmen, an island in the center of Stockholm.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The amount of destruction led to the beginning of the demolition of the Stockholm walls. Today, most of the younger city walls cannot be found anywhere above ground. However, parts of the northern city walls are preserved in the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Medieval_Stockholm" title="Museum of Medieval Stockholm">Museum of Medieval Stockholm</a>.\n</p><p>In 1710, a <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War_plague_outbreak" title="Great Northern War plague outbreak">killed about 20,000</a> (36 percent) of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> the city stagnated. Population growth halted and economic growth slowed. The city was in shock after having lost its place as the capital of a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">Great power</a>. However, Stockholm maintained its role as the political centre of Sweden and continued to develop culturally under <a href="/wiki/Gustav_III_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustav III of Sweden">Gustav III</a>.\n</p><p>By the second half of the 19th century, Stockholm had regained its leading economic role. New industries emerged and Stockholm was transformed into an important trade and service centre as well as a key gateway point within Sweden. The population also grew dramatically during this time, mainly through <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>. At the end of the 19th century, less than 40% of the residents were Stockholm-born. Settlement began to expand outside the city limits. The 19th century saw the establishment of a number of scientific institutes, including the <a href="/wiki/Karolinska_Institutet" class="mw-redirect" title="Karolinska Institutet">Karolinska Institutet</a>. The <a href="/wiki/General_Art_and_Industrial_Exposition_of_Stockholm_(1897)" class="mw-redirect" title="General Art and Industrial Exposition of Stockholm (1897)">General Art and Industrial Exposition</a> was held in 1897. From 1887 to 1953 the <a href="/wiki/Old_Stockholm_telephone_tower" title="Old Stockholm telephone tower">Old Stockholm telephone tower</a> was a landmark; originally built to link phone lines, it became redundant after these were buried, and it was latterly used for advertising.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg/220px-Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg/330px-Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg/440px-Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2487" data-file-height="1869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoghus_1-5_2007a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Centre" title="Stockholm City Centre">Stockholm City Centre</a> after the 1960s.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm became a modern, technologically advanced, and ethnically diverse city in the latter half of the 20th century. Many historical buildings were torn down during the <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernist</a> era, including substantial parts of the historical district of <a href="/wiki/Klara_(Stockholm)" title="Klara (Stockholm)">Klara</a>, and replaced with modern architecture. However, in many other parts of Stockholm (such as in <a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Gamla stan</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dermalm" title="S\xc3\xb6dermalm">S\xc3\xb6dermalm</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stermalm" title="\xc3\x96stermalm">\xc3\x96stermalm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kungsholmen" title="Kungsholmen">Kungsholmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vasastan,_Stockholm" title="Vasastan, Stockholm">Vasastan</a>), many "old" buildings, blocks and streets built before the modernism and <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_(architecture)" title="Functionalism (architecture)">functionalism</a> movements took off in Sweden (around 1930\xe2\x80\x9335) survived this era of demolition. Throughout the century, many industries shifted away from industrial activities into more high-tech and service industry areas.\n</p><p>Stockholm\'s metropolitan area is one of the fastest-growing regions in Europe, and its population is expected to number 2.5&#160;million by 2024. As a result of this massive population growth, there has been a proposal to build densely packed high-rise buildings in the city center connected by elevated walkways.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Stockholm" title="Geography of Stockholm">Geography of Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg" class="image" title="A 360 degree panorama of Stockholm inner quarters taken from the City Hall tower. From left to right: Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden with S\xc3\xb6dermalm in the background, Kungsholmen, Klara sj\xc3\xb6, Norrmalm with the central station in the foreground, Stockholms str\xc3\xb6m, Riddarholmen with the Old Town, and again Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden with S\xc3\xb6dermalm"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg/1800px-Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg" decoding="async" width="1800" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg/2700px-Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg/3600px-Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10346" data-file-height="1091" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_stadshuset.jpg" title="File:Stockholm stadshuset.jpg"> </a></div>A 360 degree panorama of Stockholm inner quarters taken from the City Hall tower. From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Riddarfj%C3%A4rden" title="Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden">Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden</a> with <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dermalm" title="S\xc3\xb6dermalm">S\xc3\xb6dermalm</a> in the background, <a href="/wiki/Kungsholmen" title="Kungsholmen">Kungsholmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klara_Sj%C3%B6" title="Klara Sj\xc3\xb6">Klara sj\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norrmalm_(proper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norrmalm (proper)">Norrmalm</a> with the central station in the foreground, <a href="/wiki/Stockholms_str%C3%B6m" title="Stockholms str\xc3\xb6m">Stockholms str\xc3\xb6m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riddarholmen" title="Riddarholmen">Riddarholmen</a> with the Old Town, and again Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden with S\xc3\xb6dermalm</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm is located on Sweden\'s east coast, where the freshwater <a href="/wiki/Lake_M%C3%A4laren" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake M\xc3\xa4laren">Lake M\xc3\xa4laren</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 Sweden\'s third-largest lake&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 flows out into the Baltic Sea. The central parts of the city consist of fourteen islands that are continuous with the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm archipelago">Stockholm archipelago</a>. The geographical city center is situated on the water, in <a href="/wiki/Riddarfj%C3%A4rden" title="Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden">Riddarfj\xc3\xa4rden</a> bay. Over 30% of the city area is made up of waterways and another 30% is made up of parks and green spaces.\n</p><p>Positioned at the eastern end of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Swedish_lowland" title="Central Swedish lowland">Central Swedish lowland</a>, the city\'s location reflect the early orientation of Swedish trade toward the Baltic region.<sup id="cite_ref-Worldregional_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldregional-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stockholm belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Temperate_deciduous_forest" title="Temperate deciduous forest">Temperate deciduous forest</a> biome, which means the climate is very similar to that of the far northeastern area of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and coastal <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The average annual temperature is 7.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (46&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The average rainfall is 531&#160;mm (21&#160;in) a year. The deciduous forest has four distinct seasons, spring, summer, autumn, and winter. In the autumn the leaves change colour. During the winter months, the trees lose their leaves.\n</p><p>For details about the other municipalities in the Stockholm area, see the pertinent articles. North of Stockholm Municipality: <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A4rf%C3%A4lla_Municipality" title="J\xc3\xa4rf\xc3\xa4lla Municipality">J\xc3\xa4rf\xc3\xa4lla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solna_Municipality" title="Solna Municipality">Solna</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A4by_Municipality" title="T\xc3\xa4by Municipality">T\xc3\xa4by</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sollentuna_Municipality" title="Sollentuna Municipality">Sollentuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liding%C3%B6_Municipality" title="Liding\xc3\xb6 Municipality">Liding\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upplands_V%C3%A4sby_Municipality" title="Upplands V\xc3\xa4sby Municipality">Upplands V\xc3\xa4sby</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96ster%C3%A5ker_Municipality" title="\xc3\x96ster\xc3\xa5ker Municipality">\xc3\x96ster\xc3\xa5ker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigtuna_Municipality" title="Sigtuna Municipality">Sigtuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundbyberg_Municipality" title="Sundbyberg Municipality">Sundbyberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danderyd_Municipality" title="Danderyd Municipality">Danderyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vallentuna_Municipality" title="Vallentuna Municipality">Vallentuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eker%C3%B6_Municipality" title="Eker\xc3\xb6 Municipality">Eker\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upplands-Bro_Municipality" title="Upplands-Bro Municipality">Upplands-Bro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vaxholm_Municipality" title="Vaxholm Municipality">Vaxholm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norrt%C3%A4lje_Municipality" title="Norrt\xc3\xa4lje Municipality">Norrt\xc3\xa4lje</a>. South of Stockholm: <a href="/wiki/Huddinge_Municipality" title="Huddinge Municipality">Huddinge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacka_Municipality" title="Nacka Municipality">Nacka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botkyrka_Municipality" title="Botkyrka Municipality">Botkyrka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haninge_Municipality" title="Haninge Municipality">Haninge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyres%C3%B6_Municipality" title="Tyres\xc3\xb6 Municipality">Tyres\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4rmd%C3%B6_Municipality" title="V\xc3\xa4rmd\xc3\xb6 Municipality">V\xc3\xa4rmd\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dert%C3%A4lje_Municipality" title="S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xa4lje Municipality">S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xa4lje</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salem_Municipality" title="Salem Municipality">Salem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nykvarn_Municipality" title="Nykvarn Municipality">Nykvarn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nyn%C3%A4shamn_Municipality" title="Nyn\xc3\xa4shamn Municipality">Nyn\xc3\xa4shamn</a>.\n</p>\n<div ESA</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg/220px-Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg/440px-Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royalpalace_Stockholm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Palace" title="Stockholm Palace">Stockholm Palace</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stockholm_Municipality">Stockholm Municipality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stockholm Municipality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Municipality" title="Stockholm Municipality">Stockholm Municipality</a></div>\n<p>Stockholm Municipality is an administrative unit defined by geographical borders. The semi-official name for the municipality is <i>City of Stockholm</i> (<i>Stockholms stad</i> in Swedish).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> As a municipality, the City of Stockholm is subdivided into district councils, which carry responsibility for primary schools, social, leisure and cultural services within their respective areas. The municipality is usually described in terms of its three main parts: Innerstaden (<a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Centre" title="Stockholm City Centre">Stockholm City Centre</a>), <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6derort" title="S\xc3\xb6derort">S\xc3\xb6derort</a> (Southern Stockholm) and <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4sterort" title="V\xc3\xa4sterort">V\xc3\xa4sterort</a> (Western Stockholm). The districts of these parts are:\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stockholm_City_Centre"><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Centre" title="Stockholm City Centre">Stockholm City Centre</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Stockholm City Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;border-bottom: dotted thin black">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Gamla stan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kungsholmen_(borough)" title="Kungsholmen (borough)">Kungsholmen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Norrmalm_(borough)" title="Norrmalm (borough)">Norrmalm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dermalm_(borough)" title="S\xc3\xb6dermalm (borough)">S\xc3\xb6dermalm</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vasastan,_Stockholm" title="Vasastan, Stockholm">Vasastan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%96stermalm_(borough)" title="\xc3\x96stermalm (borough)">\xc3\x96stermalm</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h4><span id="S.C3.B6derort"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="S\xc3\xb6derort"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6derort" title="S\xc3\xb6derort">S\xc3\xb6derort</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: S\xc3\xb6derort">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;border-bottom: dotted thin black">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Enskede-%C3%85rsta-Vant%C3%B6r" title="Enskede-\xc3\x85rsta-Vant\xc3\xb6r">Enskede-\xc3\x85rsta-Vant\xc3\xb6r</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Farsta_(borough)" title="Farsta (borough)">Farsta</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4gersten-Liljeholmen" title="H\xc3\xa4gersten-Liljeholmen">H\xc3\xa4gersten-Liljeholmen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Skarpn%C3%A4ck_(borough)" title="Skarpn\xc3\xa4ck (borough)">Skarpn\xc3\xa4ck</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sk%C3%A4rholmen_(borough)" title="Sk\xc3\xa4rholmen (borough)">Sk\xc3\xa4rholmen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%84lvsj%C3%B6_(borough)" title="\xc3\x84lvsj\xc3\xb6 (borough)">\xc3\x84lvsj\xc3\xb6</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h4><span id="V.C3.A4sterort"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="V\xc3\xa4sterort"><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4sterort" title="V\xc3\xa4sterort">V\xc3\xa4sterort</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: V\xc3\xa4sterort">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bromma" title="Bromma">Bromma</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4sselby-V%C3%A4llingby" title="H\xc3\xa4sselby-V\xc3\xa4llingby">H\xc3\xa4sselby-V\xc3\xa4llingby</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rinkeby-Kista" title="Rinkeby-Kista">Rinkeby-Kista</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sp%C3%A5nga-Tensta" title="Sp\xc3\xa5nga-Tensta">Sp\xc3\xa5nga-Tensta</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<p>The modern centre <a href="/wiki/Norrmalm_(proper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norrmalm (proper)">Norrmalm</a> (concentrated around the town square <a href="/wiki/Sergels_torg" title="Sergels torg">Sergels torg</a>) is the largest shopping district in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> It is the most central part of Stockholm in business and shopping.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> in the 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C isotherm (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen</a>: <i>Dfb</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>) in the -3&#160;\xc2\xb0C isotherm. Although winters are cold, average temperatures generally remain above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C for much of the year. Summers are pleasantly warm, and precipitation occurs throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the city\'s high northerly latitude, the length of the day varies widely from more than 18 hours around midsummer to only around 6 hours in late December. The nights from late May until mid-July are bright even when cloudy. Stockholm has relatively mild weather compared to other locations at a similar latitude, or even farther south. With an average of just over 1800 hours of sunshine per year, it is also one of the sunniest cities in Northern Europe, receiving more sunshine than Paris,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> London<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and a few other major European cities of a more southerly latitude. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a> effect and the prevailing wind traveling overland rather than sea during summer months, Stockholm has the warmest July months of the Nordic capitals. Stockholm has an annual average snow cover between 75 and 100 days.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In spite of its mild climate, Stockholm is located further north than parts of Canada that are above the Arctic <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a> at sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Summers average daytime high temperatures of 20\xe2\x80\x9325&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68\xe2\x80\x9377&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and lows of around 13&#160;\xc2\xb0C (55&#160;\xc2\xb0F), but temperatures can reach 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on some days. Days above 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) occur on average 1.55 days per year (1992\xe2\x80\x932011).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Days between 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) are relatively common especially in July and August. Night-time lows of above 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F) are rare, and hot summer nights vary from 17 to 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (63 to 64&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Winters generally bring cloudy weather with the most precipitation falling in December and January (as rain or as snow). The average winter temperatures range from \xe2\x88\x923 to \xe2\x88\x921&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27 to 30&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and occasionally drop below \xe2\x88\x9220&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x924&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in the outskirts. Spring and autumn are generally cool to mild.\n</p><p>The climate table below presents weather data from the years 1981\xe2\x80\x932010 although the official K\xc3\xb6ppen reference period was from 1961 to 1990. According to ongoing measurements, the temperature has increased during the years 1991\xe2\x80\x932009 as compared with the last series. This increase averages about 1.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (1.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F) overall months. Warming is most pronounced during the winter months, with an increase of more than 2.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (3.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in January.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> For the 2002\xe2\x80\x932014 measurements some further increases have been found, although some months such as June have been relatively flat.\n</p><p>The highest temperature ever recorded in Stockholm was 36&#160;\xc2\xb0C (97&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 3 July 1811; the lowest was \xe2\x88\x9232&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9226&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 20 January 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The temperature has not dropped to below \xe2\x88\x9225.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9213.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) since 10 January 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The warmest month ever recorded was July 2018 with a mean temperature of 22.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F) which is also the nationwide record.\n</p><p>Annual precipitation is 531&#160;mm (20.9&#160;in) with around 170 wet days and light to moderate rainfall throughout the year. The precipitation is not uniformly distributed throughout the year. The second half of the year receives 50% more than the first half. Snowfall occurs mainly from December through March. Snowfall may occasionally occur in late October as well as in April.\n</p><p>In Stockholm, the <a href="/wiki/Aurora_borealis" class="mw-redirect" title="Aurora borealis">aurora borealis</a> can occasionally be observed.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data title="Sv-Stockholm.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Daylight_hours">Daylight hours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Daylight hours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm\'s location just south of the 60th parallel north means that the number of daylight hours is relatively small during winter&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 about six hours&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 while in June and the first half of July, the nights are relatively short, with about 18 hours of daylight. Around the <a href="/wiki/Summer_solstice" title="Summer solstice">summer solstice</a> the sun never reaches further below the <a href="/wiki/Horizon" title="Horizon">horizon</a> than 7.3 degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> This gives the sky a bright blue colour in summer once the sun has set because it does not get any darker than <a href="/wiki/Nautical_twilight" class="mw-redirect" title="Nautical twilight">nautical twilight</a>. Also, when looking straight up towards the <a href="/wiki/Zenith" title="Zenith">zenith</a>, few stars are visible after the sun has gone down. This is not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">midnight sun</a>, which occurs north of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>, around 7 degrees farther north.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="City_governance">City governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: City governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Municipality" title="Stockholm Municipality">Stockholm Municipality</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg/250px-R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg/375px-R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg/500px-R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2997" data-file-height="2187" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A5dsalen_2009a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The municipal council chamber (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">R\xc3\xa5dssalen</i>), inside <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Stockholm <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Sweden)" title="Municipal council (Sweden)">Municipal Council</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Stockholms kommunfullm\xc3\xa4ktige</i>) is the name of the local assembly. Its 101 councillors are elected concurrently with <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Sweden" title="Elections in Sweden">general elections</a>, held at the same time as the elections to the <a href="/wiki/Riksdag" title="Riksdag">Riksdag</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_councils_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="County councils of Sweden">county councils</a>. The Council convenes twice every month at <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a>, and the meetings are open to the public. The matters on which the councillors decide have generally already been drafted and discussed by various boards and committees. Once decisions are referred for practical implementation, the employees of the City administrations and companies take over.<sup id="cite_ref-Governance_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Governance-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The elected majority has a Mayor and eight Vice Mayors. The Mayor and each majority Vice Mayor is the head of a department, with responsibility for a particular area of operation, such as City Planning. The opposition also has four Vice Mayors, but they hold no executive power. Together the Mayor and the 12 Vice Mayors form the Council of Mayors, and they prepare matters for the City Executive Board. The Mayor holds a special position among the Vice Mayors, chairing both the Council of Mayors and the City Executive Board.<sup id="cite_ref-Governance_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Governance-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The City Executive Board (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kommunstyrelsen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kommunstyrelsen (page does not exist)">Kommunstyrelsen</a></i>) is elected by the City Council and is equivalent to a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a>. The City Executive Board renders an opinion in all matters decided by the council and bears the overall responsibility for follow-up, evaluation and execution of its decisions. The Board is also responsible for financial administration and long-term development. The City Executive Board consists of 13 members, who represent both the majority and the opposition. Its meetings are not open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-Governance_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Governance-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2018_Stockholm_municipal_election&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2018 Stockholm municipal election (page does not exist)">2018 Stockholm municipal election</a> a majority of seats in the municipal council is at present held by a centre/right-wing majority and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipal_commissioners_for_finance_of_Stockholm" title="List of municipal commissioners for finance of Stockholm">Mayor of Stockholm</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Finansborgarr\xc3\xa5d</i>) is <a href="/wiki/Anna_Konig_Jerlmyr" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Konig Jerlmyr">Anna Konig Jerlmyr</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Moderate_Party" title="Moderate Party">Moderate Party</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg/220px-Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg/330px-Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg/440px-Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kistacentralparts_Publish.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Offices in <a href="/wiki/Kista" title="Kista">Kista</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg/220px-Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg/330px-Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg/440px-Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5336" data-file-height="3562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isafjord_1_October_2015_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The vast majority of Stockholm residents work in the service industry, which accounts for roughly 85% of jobs in Stockholm. The almost total absence of heavy industry (and fossil fuel power plants) makes Stockholm one of the world\'s cleanest <a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">metropolises</a>. The last decade has seen a significant number of jobs created in <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high technology</a> companies. Large employers include <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electrolux" title="Electrolux">Electrolux</a>. A major IT centre is located in <a href="/wiki/Kista" title="Kista">Kista</a>, in northern Stockholm.\n</p><p>Stockholm is Sweden\'s financial centre. Major Swedish banks, such as <a href="/wiki/Swedbank" title="Swedbank">Swedbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handelsbanken" title="Handelsbanken">Handelsbanken</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SEB_Group" title="SEB Group">SEB</a>, are headquartered in Stockholm, as are the major insurance companies <a href="/wiki/Skandia" title="Skandia">Skandia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Folksam" title="Folksam">Folksam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Codan_A/S" title="Codan A/S">Trygg-Hansa</a>. Stockholm is also home to Sweden\'s foremost stock exchange, the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm Stock Exchange">Stockholm Stock Exchange</a> (<i>Stockholmsb\xc3\xb6rsen</i>). Additionally, about 45% of Swedish companies with more than 200 employees are headquartered in Stockholm.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Noted clothes retailer <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a> is also headquartered in the city. In recent years, tourism has played an important part in the city\'s economy. <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_County" title="Stockholm County">Stockholm County</a> is ranked as the 10th largest visitor destination in Europe, with over 10&#160;million commercial overnight stays per year. Among 44 European cities, Stockholm had the 6th highest growth in the number of nights spent in the period 2004\xe2\x80\x932008.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest companies in Stockholm, by number of employees (2017)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 27em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 9,850</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dersjukhuset" title="S\xc3\xb6dersjukhuset">S\xc3\xb6dersjukhuset</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 5,640</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">Nordea</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 4,400</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 4,390</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SEB_Group" title="SEB Group">SEB</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 4,160</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Handelsbanken" title="Handelsbanken">Handelsbanken</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 3,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Skanska" title="Skanska">Skanska</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 2,780</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Keolis" title="Keolis">Keolis</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 2,650</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Securitas_AB" title="Securitas AB">Securitas AB</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 2,250</li>\n<li>JAG Personlig assistans &#160;\xe2\x80\x94 2,060</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/MTR_Corporation" title="MTR Corporation">MTR</a> &#160;\xe2\x80\x94 2,050</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/PostNord_Sverige" title="PostNord Sverige">Postnord</a> &#160;\xe2\x80\x942,020</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fibre_optic_network">Fibre optic network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fibre optic network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The city-owned company Stokab started in 1994 to build a fiber-optic network throughout the municipality as a level playing field for all operators (City of Stockholm, 2011). Around a decade later, the network was 1.2&#160;million kilometres (0.7&#160;million miles) long making it the longest optic fiber network in the world and now has over 90 operators and 450 enterprises as customers. 2011 was the final year of a three-year project which brought fiber to 100% of public housing, meaning an extra 95,000 houses were added. (City of Stockholm, 2011)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Stockholm" title="Education in Stockholm">Education in Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sse_north_side.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sse_north_side.jpg/220px-Sse_north_side.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sse_north_side.jpg/330px-Sse_north_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sse_north_side.jpg/440px-Sse_north_side.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sse_north_side.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_School_of_Economics" title="Stockholm School of Economics">Stockholm School of Economics</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Research and higher education in the sciences started in Stockholm in the 18th century, with education in medicine and various research institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Observatory" title="Stockholm Observatory">Stockholm Observatory</a>. The medical education was eventually formalized in 1811 as <a href="/wiki/Karolinska_Institute" title="Karolinska Institute">Karolinska Institutet</a>. <a href="/wiki/KTH_Royal_Institute_of_Technology" title="KTH Royal Institute of Technology">KTH Royal Institute of Technology</a> (<i>Swedish: Kungliga Tekniska h\xc3\xb6gskolan</i>) was founded in 1827 and is Scandinavia\'s largest higher education institute of technology with 13,000 students. <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_University" title="Stockholm University">Stockholm University</a>, founded in 1878 with university status granted in 1960, has 52,000 students as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. It also incorporates historical institutions, such as the Observatory, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Swedish Museum of Natural History">Swedish Museum of Natural History</a>, and the botanical garden <i><a href="/wiki/Bergianska_tr%C3%A4dg%C3%A5rden" title="Bergianska tr\xc3\xa4dg\xc3\xa5rden">Bergianska tr\xc3\xa4dg\xc3\xa5rden</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_School_of_Economics" title="Stockholm School of Economics">Stockholm School of Economics</a>, founded in 1909, is one of the few private institutions of higher education in Sweden.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">fine arts</a>, educational institutions include the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music,_Stockholm" title="Royal College of Music, Stockholm">Royal College of Music</a>, which has a history going back to the conservatory founded as part of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Music" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Music">Royal Swedish Academy of Music</a> in 1771, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_Art" title="Royal Institute of Art">Royal University College of Fine Arts</a>, which has a similar historical association with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Arts">Royal Swedish Academy of Arts</a> and a foundation date of 1735, and the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_National_Academy_of_Mime_and_Acting" title="Swedish National Academy of Mime and Acting">Swedish National Academy of Mime and Acting</a>, which is the continuation of the school of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dramatic_Theatre" title="Royal Dramatic Theatre">Royal Dramatic Theatre</a>, once attended by <a href="/wiki/Greta_Garbo" title="Greta Garbo">Greta Garbo</a>. Other schools include the design school <a href="/wiki/Konstfack" title="Konstfack">Konstfack</a>, founded in 1844, the <a href="/wiki/University_College_of_Opera" title="University College of Opera">University College of Opera</a> (founded in 1968 but with older roots), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dance_and_Circus" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Dance and Circus">University College of Dance</a>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Stockholms_Musikpedagogiska_Institut" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholms Musikpedagogiska Institut">Stockholms Musikpedagogiska Institut</a></i> (the University College of Music Education).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dert%C3%B6rn_College" class="mw-redirect" title="S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xb6rn College">S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xb6rn University College</a> was founded in 1995 as a multi-disciplinary institution for southern <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Stockholm" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Stockholm">Metropolitan Stockholm</a>, to balance the many institutions located in the northern part of the region.\n</p><p>Other institutes of higher education are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Military_Academy_Karlberg" title="Military Academy Karlberg">Military Academy Karlberg</a>, the world\'s oldest military academy to remain in its original location, inaugurated in 1792 and housed in <a href="/wiki/Karlberg_Palace" title="Karlberg Palace">Karlberg Palace</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ersta_Sk%C3%B6ndal_University_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Ersta Sk\xc3\xb6ndal University College">Ersta Sk\xc3\xb6ndal University College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_School_of_Theology" title="Stockholm School of Theology">Stockholm School of Theology</a> (<i>Teologiska H\xc3\xb6gskolan, Stockholm</i>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_School_of_Sport_and_Health_Sciences" title="Swedish School of Sport and Health Sciences">Swedish School of Sport and Health Sciences</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Defence_University" title="Swedish Defence University">Swedish Defence University</a></li></ul>\n<p>The biggest complaint from students of higher education in Stockholm is the lack of student accommodations, the difficulty in finding other accommodations and the high rent.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span colspan="2" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: Stockholms Stads Utrednings- och Statistikkontor AB <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.stockholmskallan.se/PostFiles/USK/historisk_befolkning_web.pdf">Befolkningen i Stockholm 1252\xe2\x80\x932005</a>, p. 55</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Stockholm region is home to around 22% of Sweden\'s total population, and accounts for about 29% of its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The geographical notion of "Stockholm" has changed over time. By the turn of the 19th century, Stockholm largely consisted of the area today known as City Centre, roughly 35&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (14&#160;sq&#160;mi) or one-fifth of the current municipal area. In the ensuing decades several other areas were incorporated (such as <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A4nnkyrka" title="Br\xc3\xa4nnkyrka">Br\xc3\xa4nnkyrka</a> Municipality in 1913, at which time it had 25,000 inhabitants, and <a href="/wiki/Sp%C3%A5nga" title="Sp\xc3\xa5nga">Sp\xc3\xa5nga</a> in 1949). The municipal border was established in 1971; with the exception of Hansta, in 1982 purchased by Stockholm Municipality from Sollentuna Municipality and today a nature reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-SthlmStatistic2006_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SthlmStatistic2006-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="float:right;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td title="Norway">Norway</a></td>\n<td>3,002\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Of the population of 935,619 in 2016, 461,677 were men and 473,942 women. The average age is 40 years; 40.1% of the population is between 20 and 44 years. 382,887 people, or 40.9% of the population, over the age 15 were unmarried. 259,153 people, or 27.7% of the population, were married. 99,524 or 10.6% of the population, had been married but divorced. 299,925 people or 32.1% of Stockholm\'s residents are of an immigrant or non-Swedish background<b>.</b><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of October 2018, there were 201,821 foreign-born people in Stockholm. The largest group of them are the <a href="/wiki/Finns" title="Finns">Finns</a> (17,000), followed by <a href="/wiki/Iraqis" title="Iraqis">Iraqis</a> (16,275), <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> (11,994) and Iranians (11,429).\n</p><p>Residents of Stockholm are known as Stockholmers ("<i>stockholmare</i>"). Languages spoken in Greater Stockholm outside of Swedish include Finnish, one of the <a href="/wiki/Official_minority_languages_of_Sweden" title="Official minority languages of Sweden">official minority languages of Sweden</a>; and English, as well as Albanian, Bosnian, Syriac, Arabic, Turkish, Kurdish, Persian, Dutch, Spanish, Serbian and Croatian.\n</p><p>The entire <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm metropolitan area">Stockholm metropolitan area</a>, consisting of 26 municipalities, has a population of over 2.2&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-scb2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scb2-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> making it the most populous city in the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nordic_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nordic-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_urban_area" title="Stockholm urban area">Stockholm urban area</a>, defined only for statistical purposes, had a total population of 1,630,738 in 2015. In the following <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Sweden" title="Municipalities of Sweden">municipalities</a> some of the districts are contained within the Stockholm urban area, though not all:<sup id="cite_ref-ne_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ne-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StockholmUrbanArea_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StockholmUrbanArea-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table style="margin: 0 auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<caption>Stockholm urban area href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Apart from being Sweden\'s capital, Stockholm houses many national cultural institutions. The Stockholm region is home to three of Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 spots judged as invaluable places that belong to all of humanity: The <a href="/wiki/Drottningholm_Palace" title="Drottningholm Palace">Drottningholm Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skogskyrkog%C3%A5rden" title="Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden">Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden</a> (The Woodland Cemetery) and <a href="/wiki/Birka" title="Birka">Birka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Drottningholm_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drottningholm-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, Stockholm was named <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Authors connected to Stockholm include the poet and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Carl_Michael_Bellman" title="Carl Michael Bellman">Carl Michael Bellman</a> (1740\xe2\x80\x931795), novelist and dramatist <a href="/wiki/August_Strindberg" title="August Strindberg">August Strindberg</a> (1849\xe2\x80\x931912), and novelist <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_S%C3%B6derberg" title="Hjalmar S\xc3\xb6derberg">Hjalmar S\xc3\xb6derberg</a> (1869\xe2\x80\x931941), all of whom made Stockholm part of their works.\n</p><p>Martin Beck is a fictional Swedish police detective from Stockholm, who is the main character in a series of 10 novels by Maj Sj\xc3\xb6wall and Per Wahl\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb6, collectively titled The Story of a Crime, and often based in Stockholm.\n</p><p>Other authors with notable heritage in Stockholm were the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize laureate</a> <a href="/wiki/Eyvind_Johnson" title="Eyvind Johnson">Eyvind Johnson</a> (1900\xe2\x80\x931976) and the popular poet and composer <a href="/wiki/Evert_Taube" title="Evert Taube">Evert Taube</a> (1890\xe2\x80\x931976). The novelist <a href="/wiki/Per_Anders_Fogelstr%C3%B6m" title="Per Anders Fogelstr\xc3\xb6m">Per Anders Fogelstr\xc3\xb6m</a> (1917\xe2\x80\x931998) wrote a popular series of historical novels depicting life in Stockholm from the mid-18th to the mid-20th century.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_Port.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Stockholm_Port.jpg/180px-Stockholm_Port.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Stockholm_Port.jpg/270px-Stockholm_Port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Stockholm_Port.jpg/360px-Stockholm_Port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_Port.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Strandv\xc3\xa4gen as seen from the island of <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Djurgardsbron_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Djurgardsbron_2008.jpg/180px-Djurgardsbron_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="133" class="thumbimage"
