class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Djurgardsbron_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rdsbron" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rdsbron">Djurg\xc3\xa5rdsbron</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg/180px-Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg/270px-Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg/360px-Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="516" data-file-height="420" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholms-stadsbibliotek-2003-04-14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Public_Library" title="Stockholm Public Library">Stockholm Public Library</a>, designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Gunnar_Asplund" title="Gunnar Asplund">Gunnar Asplund</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_in_Stockholm" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecture in Stockholm">Architecture in Stockholm</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Historical_fires_of_Stockholm" title="Historical fires of Stockholm">Historical fires of Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Look_from_Erricson_globe,_stockholm.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png/220px-Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png/330px-Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png/440px-Look_from_Erricson_globe%2C_stockholm.png 2x" data-file-width="1612" data-file-height="906" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Look_from_Erricson_globe,_stockholm.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Look at Stockholm from <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_Globe" title="Ericsson Globe">Ericsson Globe</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The city\'s oldest section is Gamla stan (Old Town), located on the original small islands of the city\'s earliest settlements and still featuring the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> street layout. Some notable buildings of Gamla Stan are the large German Church (<i>Tyska kyrkan</i>) and several mansions and palaces: the <i><a href="/wiki/Swedish_House_of_Nobility" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish House of Nobility">Riddarhuset</a></i> (the House of Nobility), the <a href="/wiki/Bonde_Palace" title="Bonde Palace">Bonde Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tessin_Palace" title="Tessin Palace">Tessin Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Axel_Oxenstierna_palace" title="Axel Oxenstierna palace">Oxenstierna Palace</a>.\n</p><p>The oldest building in Stockholm is the <a href="/wiki/Riddarholm_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Riddarholm Church">Riddarholmskyrkan</a> from the late 13th century. After a fire in 1697 when the original medieval castle was destroyed, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Palace" title="Stockholm Palace">Stockholm Palace</a> was erected in a <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> style. <a href="/wiki/Storkyrkan" title="Storkyrkan">Storkyrkan</a> Cathedral, the episcopal seat of the Bishop of Stockholm, stands next to the castle. It was founded in the 13th century but is clad in a baroque exterior dating to the 18th century.\n</p><p>As early as the 15th century, the city had expanded outside of its original borders. Some pre-industrial, small-scale buildings from this era can still be found in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dermalm" title="S\xc3\xb6dermalm">S\xc3\xb6dermalm</a>. During the 19th century and the age of industrialization Stockholm grew rapidly, with plans and architecture inspired by the large cities of the continent such as <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. Notable works of this time period include public buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Opera" title="Royal Swedish Opera">Royal Swedish Opera</a> and private developments such as the luxury housing developments on <a href="/wiki/Strandv%C3%A4gen" title="Strandv\xc3\xa4gen">Strandv\xc3\xa4gen</a>.\n</p><p>In the 20th century, a nationalistic push spurred a new architectural style inspired by medieval and renaissance ancestry as well as influences of the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Jugend</a>/Art Nouveau style. A key landmark of Stockholm, the Stockholm City Hall, was erected 1911\xe2\x80\x931923 by architect <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_%C3%96stberg" title="Ragnar \xc3\x96stberg">Ragnar \xc3\x96stberg</a>. Other notable works of these times are the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Public_Library" title="Stockholm Public Library">Stockholm Public Library</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> <a href="/wiki/Skogskyrkog%C3%A5rden" title="Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden">Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skogskyrkog\xc3\xa5rden-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sodertornet_at_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sodertornet_at_night.jpg/180px-Sodertornet_at_night.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sodertornet_at_night.jpg/270px-Sodertornet_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sodertornet_at_night.jpg/360px-Sodertornet_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1927" data-file-height="2953" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sodertornet_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6der_Torn" title="S\xc3\xb6der Torn">S\xc3\xb6der Torn</a>, an 86-metre-tall (282-foot) building in S\xc3\xb6dermalm.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1930s modernism characterized the development of the city as it grew. New residential areas sprang up such as the development on <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A4rdet" title="G\xc3\xa4rdet">G\xc3\xa4rdet</a> while industrial development added to the growth, such as the KF manufacturing industries on Kvarnholmen located in the Nacka Municipality. In the 1950s, suburban development entered a new phase with the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_metro" title="Stockholm metro">Stockholm metro</a>. The modernist developments of <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4llingby" title="V\xc3\xa4llingby">V\xc3\xa4llingby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farsta" title="Farsta">Farsta</a> were internationally praised. In the 1960s this suburban development continued but with the aesthetic of the times, the industrialized and mass-produced blocks of flats received a large amount of criticism.\n</p><p>At the same time that this suburban development was taking place, the most central areas of the inner city were being redesigned, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Redevelopment_of_Norrmalm" title="Redevelopment of Norrmalm">Norrmalmsregleringen</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Sergels_Torg" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergels Torg">Sergels Torg</a>, with its five high-rise office towers was created in the 1960s, followed by the total clearance of large areas to make room for new development projects. The most notable buildings from this period include the ensemble of the <a href="/wiki/The_House_of_Culture_(Stockholm)" title="The House of Culture (Stockholm)">House of Culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Theatre" title="Stockholm City Theatre">City Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Riksbank</a> at Sergels Torg, designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Peter_Celsing" title="Peter Celsing">Peter Celsing</a>.\n</p><p>In the 1980s, the planning ideas of modernism were starting to be questioned, resulting in suburbs with denser planning, such as <a href="/wiki/Skarpn%C3%A4ck_(borough)" title="Skarpn\xc3\xa4ck (borough)">Skarpn\xc3\xa4ck</a>. In the 1990s this idea was taken further with the development of an old industrial area close to the inner city, resulting in a sort of mix of modernistic and urban planning<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in the new area of <a href="/wiki/Hammarby_Sj%C3%B6stad" title="Hammarby Sj\xc3\xb6stad">Hammarby Sj\xc3\xb6stad</a>.\n</p><p>The municipality has appointed an official "board of beauty" called "<a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Beauty_Council" title="Stockholm Beauty Council">Sk\xc3\xb6nhetsr\xc3\xa5det</a>" to protect and preserve the beauty of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stockholm\'s architecture (along with Visby, <a href="/wiki/Gotland" title="Gotland">Gotland</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>) provided the inspiration for Japanese <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> director <a href="/wiki/Hayao_Miyazaki" title="Hayao Miyazaki">Hayao Miyazaki</a> as he sought to evoke an idealized city untouched by World War. His creation called <i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Koriko</a></i>, draws directly from what Miyazaki felt was Stockholm\'s sense of well-established architectural unity, vibrancy, independence, and safety.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Stockholm" title="List of museums in Stockholm">List of museums in Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg/220px-Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg/330px-Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg/440px-Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vasa_Museum_interior1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main hall of the <a href="/wiki/Vasa_Museum" title="Vasa Museum">Vasa Museum</a> with a scale model of Vasa as it might have looked on its maiden voyage to the left and the preserved <a href="/wiki/Vasa_(ship)" title="Vasa (ship)">ship itself</a> to the right</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg/220px-Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg/330px-Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg/440px-Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morag%C3%A5rden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Morag\xc3\xa5rden, one of many historical <a href="/wiki/Homestead_(buildings)" title="Homestead (buildings)">homesteads</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Skansen" title="Skansen">Skansen</a> <a href="/wiki/Open-air_museum" title="Open-air museum">open-air museum</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm is one of the most crowded museum-cities in the world with around 100 museums, visited by millions of people every year.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Vasa_Museum" title="Vasa Museum">Vasa Museum</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Vasamuseet</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Maritime_museum" title="Maritime museum">maritime museum</a> on <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden</a> which displays the only almost fully intact 17th century <a href="/wiki/Ship" title="Ship">ship</a> that has ever been salvaged, the 64-gun warship <i><a href="/wiki/Vasa_(ship)" title="Vasa (ship)">Vasa</a></i> that sank on her <a href="/wiki/Maiden_voyage" class="mw-redirect" title="Maiden voyage">maiden voyage</a> in 1628.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nationalmuseum" title="Nationalmuseum">Nationalmuseum</a> houses the largest collection of art in the country: 16,000 paintings and 30,000 objects of art handicraft. The collection dates back to the days of Gustav Vasa in the 16th century, and has since been expanded with works by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Antoine_Watteau" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-Antoine Watteau">Antoine Watteau</a>, as well as constituting a main part of Sweden\'s art heritage, manifested in the works of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Roslin" title="Alexander Roslin">Alexander Roslin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anders_Zorn" title="Anders Zorn">Anders Zorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johan_Tobias_Sergel" title="Johan Tobias Sergel">Johan Tobias Sergel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Larsson" title="Carl Larsson">Carl Larsson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Fredrik_Hill" title="Carl Fredrik Hill">Carl Fredrik Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Josephson" title="Ernst Josephson">Ernst Josephson</a>. From the year 2013 to 2018 the museum was closed due to a restoration of the building.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Moderna_Museet" title="Moderna Museet">Moderna Museet</a> (Museum of Modern Art) is Sweden\'s national museum of <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a>. It has works by noted modern artists such as <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Picasso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dal\xc3\xad">Salvador Dal\xc3\xad</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Skansen" title="Skansen">Skansen</a> (in English: the <a href="/wiki/Sconce_(fortification)" title="Sconce (fortification)">Sconce</a>) is a combined <a href="/wiki/Open-air_museum" title="Open-air museum">open-air museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoo</a>, located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden</a>. It was founded in 1891 by <a href="/wiki/Artur_Hazelius" title="Artur Hazelius">Artur Hazelius</a> (1833\xe2\x80\x931901) to show the way of life in the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Sweden" title="Provinces of Sweden">different parts of Sweden</a> before the industrial era.\n</p><p>Other notable museums (in alphabetical order):\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ABBA:_The_Museum" title="ABBA: The Museum">ABBA: The Museum</a>, an interactive exhibit about the pop-group <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fotografiska" title="Fotografiska">Fotografiska</a>, museum of photography</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Livrustkammaren" title="Livrustkammaren">Livrustkammaren</a>, the royal armoury, located at <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Palace" title="Stockholm Palace">Stockholm Palace</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Museum">Nobel Museum</a>, devoted to the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>, and the founder of the prize, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a> (1833\xe2\x80\x931896)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nordic_Museum" title="Nordic Museum">Nordic Museum</a>, dedicated to the cultural history and ethnography of Sweden</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Coin_Cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Coin Cabinet">Royal Coin Cabinet</a>, dedicated to the history of money and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">economic history</a> in general</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Museum" title="Stockholm City Museum">Stockholm City Museum</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Swedish Museum of Natural History">Swedish Museum of Natural History</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_galleries">Art galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Art galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm has a vibrant art scene with a number of internationally recognized art centres and commercial galleries. Amongst others, privately sponsored initiatives such as <a href="/wiki/Bonnier_Group" title="Bonnier Group">Bonniers</a> Konsthall, Magasin 3, and state-supported institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Tensta_Konsthall" title="Tensta Konsthall">Tensta Konsthall</a> and Index all show leading international and national artists. In the last few years, a gallery district has emerged around Hudiksvallsgatan where leading galleries such as Andr\xc3\xa9hn-Schiptjenko, Br\xc3\xa4ndstr\xc3\xb6m &amp; Stene have located. Other important commercial galleries include Nordenhake, <a href="/wiki/Milliken_Gallery" title="Milliken Gallery">Milliken Gallery</a> and Galleri Magnus Karlsson.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suburbs">Suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Stockholm suburbs are places with diverse cultural background. Some areas in the inner suburbs, including those of <a href="/wiki/Sk%C3%A4rholmen" title="Sk\xc3\xa4rholmen">Sk\xc3\xa4rholmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tensta" title="Tensta">Tensta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordbro" title="Jordbro">Jordbro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fittja" title="Fittja">Fittja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Husby,_Stockholm" title="Husby, Stockholm">Husby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandbergen" title="Brandbergen">Brandbergen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinkeby" title="Rinkeby">Rinkeby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rissne" title="Rissne">Rissne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kista" title="Kista">Kista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hags%C3%A4tra" title="Hags\xc3\xa4tra">Hags\xc3\xa4tra</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4sselby" title="H\xc3\xa4sselby">H\xc3\xa4sselby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farsta_(borough)" title="Farsta (borough)">Farsta</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A5gsved" title="R\xc3\xa5gsved">R\xc3\xa5gsved</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flemingsberg" title="Flemingsberg">Flemingsberg</a>, and the outer suburb of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dert%C3%A4lje" title="S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xa4lje">S\xc3\xb6dert\xc3\xa4lje</a>, have high percentages of immigrants or second generation immigrants. These mainly come from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> (Assyrians, Syriacs, Turks and Kurds) also Bosnians and Serbs, but there are also immigrants from Africa, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Other parts of the inner suburbs, such as T\xc3\xa4by, Danderyd, Liding\xc3\xb6, Nacka, <a href="/wiki/Flysta" title="Flysta">Flysta</a> and, as well as some of the suburbs mentioned above, have a majority of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedes</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dramaten_050701.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dramaten_050701.JPG/220px-Dramaten_050701.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dramaten_050701.JPG/330px-Dramaten_050701.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dramaten_050701.JPG/440px-Dramaten_050701.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1021" data-file-height="843" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dramaten_050701.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Royal_Dramatic_Theatre" title="Royal Dramatic Theatre">Royal Dramatic Theatre</a>, one of Stockholm\'s many theatres.</div></div></div>\n<p>Distinguished among Stockholm\'s many theatres are the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dramatic_Theatre" title="Royal Dramatic Theatre">Royal Dramatic Theatre</a> (<i>Kungliga Dramatiska Teatern</i>), one of Europe\'s most renowned theatres, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Opera" title="Royal Swedish Opera">Royal Swedish Opera</a>, inaugurated in 1773.\n</p><p>Other notable theatres are the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Theatre" title="Stockholm City Theatre">Stockholm City Theatre</a> (Stockholms stadsteater), the Peoples Opera (<i><a href="/wiki/Folkoperan" title="Folkoperan">Folkoperan</a></i>), the Modern Theatre of Dance (<i>Moderna dansteatern</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Chinateatern" title="Chinateatern">China Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ta_Lejon" title="G\xc3\xb6ta Lejon">G\xc3\xb6ta Lejon</a> Theatre, the <a href="/wiki/Mosebacke" title="Mosebacke">Mosebacke</a> Theatre, and the <a href="/wiki/Oscarsteatern" title="Oscarsteatern">Oscar Theatre</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Amusement_park">Amusement park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Amusement park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%B6na_Lund" title="Gr\xc3\xb6na Lund">Gr\xc3\xb6na Lund</a> is an amusement park located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden</a>. This amusement park has over 30 attractions and many restaurants. It is a popular tourist attraction and visited by thousands of people every day. It is open from the end of April to the middle of September. Gr\xc3\xb6na Lund also serves as a concert venue.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg/220px-Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg/330px-Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg/440px-Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="465" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vasabron_Riddarholmen_Norstedts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bookpublisher, <a href="/wiki/Norstedt_Building" title="Norstedt Building">Norstedt Building</a>, seen from <a href="/wiki/Vasabron" title="Vasabron">Vasabron</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Riddarholmen" title="Riddarholmen">Riddarholmen</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm is the media centre of Sweden. It has four nationwide daily newspapers and is also the central location of the publicly funded radio (<a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Radio" title="Sveriges Radio">SR</a>) and television (<a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Television" title="Sveriges Television">SVT</a>). In addition, all other major television channels have their base in Stockholm, such as: <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Viasat)" title="TV3 (Viasat)">TV3</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV4_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="TV4 Group">TV4</a> and <a href="/wiki/TV6_(Sweden)" title="TV6 (Sweden)">TV6</a>. All major magazines are also located to Stockholm, as are the largest literature publisher, the <a href="/wiki/Bonnier_Group" title="Bonnier Group">Bonnier group</a>. The world\'s best-selling video game <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a></i> was created in Stockholm by <a href="/wiki/Markus_Persson" title="Markus Persson">Markus \'Notch\' Persson</a> in 2009, and its company <a href="/wiki/Mojang" class="mw-redirect" title="Mojang">Mojang</a> is headquartered there.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Stockholm" title="Football in Stockholm">Football in Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg/220px-Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg/330px-Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg/440px-Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Friends_Arena_from_inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Friends_Arena" title="Friends Arena">Friends Arena</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg/220px-Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg/330px-Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg/440px-Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandyfinal2010_hammarby_celebration.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scenes after <a href="/wiki/Hammarby_IF_Bandy" title="Hammarby IF Bandy">Hammarby</a> won their first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swedish_bandy_champions" title="List of Swedish bandy champions">national bandy title</a> in 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>The most popular spectator sports are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. The three most popular football clubs in Stockholm are <a href="/wiki/AIK_Fotboll" title="AIK Fotboll">AIK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rdens_IF_Fotboll" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rdens IF Fotboll">Djurg\xc3\xa5rdens IF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hammarby_Fotboll" title="Hammarby Fotboll">Hammarby IF</a>, who all play in the first tier, <a href="/wiki/Allsvenskan" title="Allsvenskan">Allsvenskan</a>. <a href="/wiki/AIK_Fotboll" title="AIK Fotboll">AIK</a> play at Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_stadiums" title="List of national stadiums">national stadium for football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friends_Arena" title="Friends Arena">Friends Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Solna_Municipality" title="Solna Municipality">Solna</a>, with a capacity of 54,329. The Europa League final of 2017 was played the 24th of May between AFC Ajax and Manchester United on Friends Arena. Manchester United won the trophy after a 2\xe2\x80\x930 victory.\n</p><p>Djurg\xc3\xa5rdens IF and <a href="/wiki/Hammarby_IF" title="Hammarby IF">Hammarby</a> play at <a href="/wiki/Tele2_Arena" title="Tele2 Arena">Tele2 Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Johanneshov" title="Johanneshov">Johanneshov</a>, with a capacity of 30,000 spectators.\n</p><p>All three clubs are multi-sport clubs, which have ice hockey teams; <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rdens_IF_Hockey" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rdens IF Hockey">Djurg\xc3\xa5rdens IF</a> play in <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Hockey_League" title="Swedish Hockey League">the first tier</a>, AIK in <a href="/wiki/HockeyAllsvenskan" title="HockeyAllsvenskan">the second</a> and Hammarby in <a href="/wiki/Hockeyettan" title="Hockeyettan">the third tier</a>, as well as teams in <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a> and other sports, including individual sports.\n</p><p>Historically, the city was the host of the <a href="/wiki/1912_Summer_Olympics" title="1912 Summer Olympics">1912 Summer Olympics</a>. From those days stem the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Olympic_Stadium" title="Stockholm Olympic Stadium">Stockholms Olympiastadion</a> which has since hosted numerous sports events, notably football and athletics. Other major sports arenas are Friends Arena the new national football stadium, <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_Globe" title="Ericsson Globe">Stockholm Globe Arena</a>, a multi-sport arena and one of the largest spherical buildings in the world and the nearby indoor arena <a href="/wiki/Hovet" title="Hovet">Hovet</a>.\n</p><p>Besides the 1912 Summer Olympics, Stockholm hosted the <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_at_the_1956_Summer_Olympics" title="Equestrian at the 1956 Summer Olympics">1956 Summer Olympics Equestrian Games</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">UEFA Euro 1992</a>. The city was also second runner up in the <a href="/wiki/Bids_for_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Bids for the 2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics bids</a>. Stockholm hosted the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 FIFA World Cup</a>. Stockholm recently bid jointly with <a href="/wiki/%C3%85re" title="\xc3\x85re">\xc3\x85re</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2026_Winter_Olympics" title="2026 Winter Olympics">2026 Winter Olympics</a> but lost out to the joint bid of <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>/<a href="/wiki/Cortina_d%27Ampezzo" title="Cortina d&#39;Ampezzo">Cortina d\'Ampezzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, if awarded it would have been the second city to host both Summer and Winter Olympics after <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/2026_Winter_Paralympics" title="2026 Winter Paralympics">2026 Winter Paralympics</a> and with <a href="/wiki/%C3%85re" title="\xc3\x85re">\xc3\x85re</a> it would have also be to host all three winter event including <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winter_Paralympic_Games" title="Winter Paralympic Games">Winter Paralympic Games</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics_World_Games" title="Special Olympics World Games">Special Olympics World Winter Games</a> in which <a href="/wiki/%C3%85re" title="\xc3\x85re">\xc3\x85re</a> would have host in 2021 along with <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stersund" title="\xc3\x96stersund">\xc3\x96stersund</a>, however Sweden pulled out host the Special Olympic World Winter Games 2021 due to lack of funding instead it moved to <a href="/wiki/Kazan" title="Kazan">Kazan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and was delayed to 2022. Stockholm first bid for the Winter Olympics for <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a>, but withdrew its bid in 2014 due to financial matters.\n</p><p>Stockholm also hosted all but one of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Games" title="Nordic Games">Nordic Games</a>, a winter <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> that predated the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a>.\n</p><p>In 2015, the Stockholms Kungar <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> club was formed. They are Stockholm\'s first Rugby league team and will play in Sweden\'s National Rugby league championship.\n</p><p>Every year Stockholm is host to the \xc3\x96TILL\xc3\x96 Swimrun World Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stockholm has hosted the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Open" title="Stockholm Open">Stockholm Open</a>, an <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_250_series" class="mw-redirect" title="ATP World Tour 250 series">ATP World Tour 250 series</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> tournament annually since 1969. Each year since 1995, the tournament has been hosted at the <a href="/wiki/Kungliga_tennishallen" title="Kungliga tennishallen">Kungliga tennishallen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are over 1000 restaurants in Stockholm.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Stockholm boasts a total of ten <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin star</a> restaurants, two with two stars and one with three stars.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yearly_events_and_Festivals">Yearly events and Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Yearly events and Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_Marathon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stockholm_Marathon.jpg/220px-Stockholm_Marathon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stockholm_Marathon.jpg/330px-Stockholm_Marathon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stockholm_Marathon.jpg/440px-Stockholm_Marathon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_Marathon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Marathon" title="Stockholm Marathon">Stockholm Marathon</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Kungstr%C3%A4dg%C3%A5rden" title="Kungstr\xc3\xa4dg\xc3\xa5rden">Kungstr\xc3\xa4dg\xc3\xa5rden</a> in 2008</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Jazz_Festival" title="Stockholm Jazz Festival">Stockholm Jazz Festival</a> is one of Sweden\'s oldest festivals. The festival takes place at Skeppsholmen in July.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Early_Music_Festival" title="Stockholm Early Music Festival">Stockholm Early Music Festival</a>, the largest international event for historical music in the Nordic countries. First week in June since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Culture_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stockholm Culture Festival (page does not exist)">Stockholm Culture Festival</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swe</a>: <i>Stockholms kulturfestival</i>) is a free recurring cultural festival in August, which is held by the City of Stockholm. Runs in parallel with We Are Stockholm. <sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/We_Are_Sthlm" title="We Are Sthlm">We Are Stockholm</a> is a free youth festival people between 13 and 19 years. Runs in parallel with the Stockholm Culture Festival in August and is held by the City of Stockholm. Between 2001 -2013, the festival went by the name Ung08.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Pride" title="Stockholm Pride">Stockholm Pride</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">Pride</a> event in the Nordic countries and takes place in the last week of July every year. The Stockholm Pride festival always ends with a parade and in 2007, 50,000 people marched with the parade and about 500,000 watched.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Marathon" title="Stockholm Marathon">Stockholm Marathon</a> takes place on a Saturday in early June each year.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Banquet</a> takes place at <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a> every year on 10 December.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Water_Festival" title="Stockholm Water Festival">Stockholm Water Festival</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swe</a>: <i>Vattenfestivalen</i>) was a popular summer <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">festival</a> held annually in Stockholm between 1991 and 1999.</li>\n<li>Manifestation, a yearly ecumenical Christian festival with up to 25,000 participants.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Summerburst&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Summerburst (page does not exist)">Summerburst Music festival</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Film_Festival" title="Stockholm International Film Festival">The Stockholm International Film Festival</a> is an annual film festival held in Stockholm each year since 1990.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg/220px-Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg/330px-Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg/440px-Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="620" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkudden_djurgarden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Park on the island of <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden</a> in central Stockholm.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_city_with_a_national_urban_park">Green city with a national urban park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Green city with a national urban park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm is one of the cleanest capitals in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The city was granted the 2010 <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital_Award" title="European Green Capital Award">European Green Capital Award</a> by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">EU Commission</a>; this was Europe\'s first "green capital".<sup id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Applicant cities were evaluated in several ways: climate change, local transport, public green areas, air quality, noise, waste, water consumption, waste water treatment, sustainable utilisation of land, biodiversity and environmental management.<sup id="cite_ref-international.stockholm.se_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international.stockholm.se-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Out of 35 participant cities, eight finalists were chosen: Stockholm, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_im_Breisgau" title="Freiburg im Breisgau">Freiburg</a>, Hamburg, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="M\xc3\xbcnster">M\xc3\xbcnster</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-August_2010_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-August_2010-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Some of the reasons why Stockholm won the 2010 European Green Capital Award were: its integrated administrative system, which ensures that environmental aspects are considered in budgets, operational planning, reporting, and monitoring; its cut in carbon dioxide emissions by 25% per capita in ten years; and its decision towards being fossil fuel free by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-international.stockholm.se_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international.stockholm.se-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Stockholm has long demonstrated concern for the environment. The city\'s environmental program is the fifth since the first one was established in the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Stockholm passed the title of European Green Capital to Hamburg, Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-August_2010_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-August_2010-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_model">Role model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Role model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the beginning of 2010, Stockholm launched the program Professional Study Visits<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> in order to share the city\'s green best practices. The program provides visitors with the opportunity to learn how to address issues such as waste management, urban planning, carbon dioxide emissions, and sustainable and efficient transportation system, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the European Cities Monitor 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Stockholm is the best city in terms of freedom from pollution. Surrounded by 219 nature reserves, Stockholm has around 1,000 green spaces, which corresponds to 30% of the city\'s area.<sup id="cite_ref-Environment_2010_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environment_2010-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Founded in 1995, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_City_Park" title="Royal National City Park">Royal National City Park</a> is the world\'s first legally protected "national urban park".<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> For a description of the formation process, value assets and implementation of the legal protection of The Royal National Urban Park, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gih.diva-portal.org/smash/record.jsf?searchId=1&amp;pid=diva2:528">Schantz 2006</a> The water in Stockholm is so clean that people can dive and fish in the centre of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Environment_2010_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environment_2010-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The waters of downtown Stockholm serve as spawning grounds for multiple fish species including trout and salmon, though human intervention is needed to keep populations up.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Regarding CO2 emissions, the government\'s target is that Stockholm will be CO2 free before 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-Environment_2010_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environment_2010-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_quality">Air quality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Air quality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm used to have problematic levels of particulates (PM10) due to studded winter tires, but as of 2016 the levels are below limits, after street-specific bans. Instead the current (2016) problem is nitrogen oxides emitted by diesel vehicles. In 2016 the average levels for urban background (roof of Torkel Knutssonsgatan) were: <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide" title="Nitrogen dioxide">NO<sub>2</sub></a> 11 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NO<sub>x</sub></a> 14 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">PM10</a> 12 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, PM2.5 4.9 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Soot" title="Soot">soot</a> 0.4 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Ultrafine_particle" title="Ultrafine particle">ultrafine particles</a> 6200/cm<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">CO</a> 0.2&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">SO<sub>2</sub></a> 0.4 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> 51 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>. For urban street level (the densely trafficked Hornsgatan) the average levels were: NO<sub>2</sub> 43 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, NO<sub>x</sub> 104 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, PM10 23 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, PM2.5 5.9 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, soot 1.0 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>, ultrafine particles 17100/cm<sup>3</sup>, CO 0.3&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>, ozone 31 \xce\xbcg/m<sup>3</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Transportation">Public Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Public Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Stockholm" title="Public transport in Stockholm">Public transport in Stockholm</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SL_C20_Gamla_Stan,_Stockholm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg/220px-SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg/330px-SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg/440px-SL_C20_Gamla_Stan%2C_Stockholm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5363" data-file-height="3311" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SL_C20_Gamla_Stan,_Stockholm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A southbound full-length (3 car) <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_C20" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier C20">C20 metrotrain</a> departing from the <a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan_metro_station" title="Gamla stan metro station">Gamla stan station</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm has an extensive <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> system. It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm Metro">Stockholm Metro</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Tunnelbanan</i>), which consist of three color-coded main systems (green, red and blue) with seven lines (10, 11, 13, 14, 17, 18, 19); the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_commuter_rail" title="Stockholm commuter rail">Stockholm commuter rail</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Pendelt\xc3\xa5gen</i>) which runs on the state-owned railroads on six lines (40, 41, 42, 43, 44, 48); four <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Stockholm" title="Trams in Stockholm">light rail/tramway lines</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sp%C3%A5rv%C3%A4g_City" title="Sp\xc3\xa5rv\xc3\xa4g City">7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nockebybanan" title="Nockebybanan">12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liding%C3%B6banan" title="Liding\xc3\xb6banan">21</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tv%C3%A4rbanan" title="Tv\xc3\xa4rbanan">22</a>); the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_three_foot_gauge_railways" title="Swedish three foot gauge railways">891 mm</a> <a href="/wiki/Narrow-gauge_railway" title="Narrow-gauge railway">narrow-gauge railway</a> <a href="/wiki/Roslagsbanan" title="Roslagsbanan">Roslagsbanan</a>, on three lines (27, 28, 29) in the northeastern part; the local railway <a href="/wiki/Saltsj%C3%B6banan" title="Saltsj\xc3\xb6banan">Saltsj\xc3\xb6banan</a>, on two lines (25, 26) in the southeastern part; a large number of bus lines, and the inner-city <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rden_ferry" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rden ferry">Djurg\xc3\xa5rden ferry</a>. The overwhelming majority of the land-based public transport in Stockholm County (save for the airport buses/<a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Express" title="Arlanda Express">airport express trains</a> and other few commercially viable bus lines) is organized under the common umbrella of <a href="/wiki/Storstockholms_Lokaltrafik" title="Storstockholms Lokaltrafik">Storstockholms Lokaltrafik</a> (SL), an <a href="/wiki/Aktiebolag" title="Aktiebolag">aktiebolag</a> wholly owned by <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_County_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm County Council">Stockholm County Council</a>. Since the 1990s, the operation and maintenance of the SL public transport services are contracted out to independent companies bidding for contracts, such as <a href="/wiki/MTR_Corporation" title="MTR Corporation">MTR</a>, which operate the Metro. The archipelago boat traffic is handled by <a href="/wiki/Waxholmsbolaget" title="Waxholmsbolaget">Waxholmsbolaget</a>, which is also wholly owned by the County Council.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png/200px-Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png/300px-Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png/400px-Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png 2x" data-file-width="1548" data-file-height="1308" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_7_tram_bound_for_Sergels_Torg_in_Stockholm_Sweden.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Flexity_Classic" title="Bombardier Flexity Classic">A34 tram</a> on <a href="/wiki/Sp%C3%A5rv%C3%A4g_City" title="Sp\xc3\xa5rv\xc3\xa4g City">line 7</a> at <a href="/wiki/Djurg%C3%A5rdsbron" title="Djurg\xc3\xa5rdsbron">Djurg\xc3\xa5rdsbron</a></div></div></div>\n<p>SL has a common ticket system in the entire Stockholm County, which allows for easy travel between different modes of transport. The tickets are of two main types, single ticket and <a href="/wiki/Travel_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Travel card">travel cards</a>, both allowing for unlimited travel with SL in the entire Stockholm County for the duration of the ticket validity. On 1 April 2007, a zone system (A, B, C) and price system was introduced. Single tickets were available in forms of cash ticket, individual unit pre-paid tickets, pre-paid ticket slips of 8, sms-ticket and machine ticket. Cash tickets bought at the point of travel were the most expensive and pre-paid tickets slips of 8 are the cheapest. A single ticket costs 32 SEK with the card and 45 SEK without and is valid for 75 minutes. The duration of the travel card validity depended on the exact type; they were available from 24 hours up to a year. As of 2018, a 30-day card costs 860&#160;SEK. Tickets of all these types were available with reduced prices for students and persons under 20 and over 65 years of age. On 9 January 2017, the zone system was removed, and the cost of the tickets was increased.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_City_Line_Project">The City Line Project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: The City Line Project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Line" title="Stockholm City Line">Stockholm City Line</a></div>\n<p>With an estimated cost of SEK 16.8&#160;billion (January 2007 price level), which equals 2.44&#160;billion US dollars, the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Line" title="Stockholm City Line">City Line</a>, an environmentally certified project, comprises a 6&#160;km (3.7&#160;mi)-long commuter train tunnel (in rock and water) beneath Stockholm, with two new stations (Stockholm City and Stockholm Odenplan), and a 1.4&#160;km (0.87&#160;mi)-long railway bridge at <a href="/wiki/Enskede-%C3%85rsta" title="Enskede-\xc3\x85rsta">\xc3\x85rsta</a>. The City Line was built by the Swedish Transport Administration in co-operation with the City of Stockholm, Stockholm County Council, and Stockholm Transport, SL. As <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a> is overloaded, the purpose of this project was to double the city\'s track capacity and improve service efficiency. Operations began in July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-trafikverket1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafikverket1-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between <a href="/wiki/Riddarholmen" title="Riddarholmen">Riddarholmen</a> and S\xc3\xb6der M\xc3\xa4larstrand, the City Line runs through a submerged concrete tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-trafikverket1_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafikverket1-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> As a green project, the City Line includes the purification of waste water; noise reduction through sound-attenuating tracks; the use of synthetic diesel, which provides users with clean air; and the recycling of excavated rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-trafikverket1_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafikverket1-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg/220px-Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg/330px-Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg/440px-Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4695" data-file-height="3390" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Norra_L%C3%A4nken_nov_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Norra_l%C3%A4nken" title="Norra l\xc3\xa4nken">Norra l\xc3\xa4nken</a> (North link) motorway in Stockholm.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm is at the junction of the <a href="/wiki/International_E-road_network" title="International E-road network">European routes</a> <a href="/wiki/European_route_E4" title="European route E4">E4</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_route_E18" title="European route E18">E18</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_route_E20" title="European route E20">E20</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Ring_Road" title="Stockholm Ring Road">half-completed motorway ring road</a> exists on the south, west and north sides of the City Centre. The northern section of the ring road, Norra L\xc3\xa4nken, opened for traffic in 2015 while the final subsea eastern section is being discussed as a future project. A bypass motorway for traffic between Northern and Southern Sweden, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%B6rbifart_Stockholm" title="F\xc3\xb6rbifart Stockholm">F\xc3\xb6rbifart Stockholm</a>, is being built. The many islands and waterways make extensions of the road system both complicated and expensive, and new motorways are often built as systems of tunnels and bridges.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Congestion_charges">Congestion charges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Congestion charges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_congestion_tax" title="Stockholm congestion tax">Stockholm congestion tax</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Betalstation_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Betalstation_2010.jpg/220px-Betalstation_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Betalstation_2010.jpg/330px-Betalstation_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Betalstation_2010.jpg/440px-Betalstation_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="1725" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Betalstation_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A control point for the congestion charge leading up to <a href="/wiki/Essingeleden" title="Essingeleden">Essingeleden</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm has a <a href="/wiki/Congestion_pricing" title="Congestion pricing">congestion pricing</a> system, Stockholm congestion tax,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> in use on a permanent basis since 1 August 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> after having had a seven-month trial period in the first half of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The City Centre is within the congestion tax zone. All the entrances and exits of this area have unmanned control points operating with <a href="/wiki/Automatic_number_plate_recognition" class="mw-redirect" title="Automatic number plate recognition">automatic number plate recognition</a>. All vehicles entering or exiting the congestion tax affected area, with a few exceptions, have to pay 10\xe2\x80\x9320&#160;<a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">SEK</a> (1.09\xe2\x80\x932.18&#160;<a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">EUR</a>, 1.49\xe2\x80\x932.98&#160;<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>) depending on the time of day between 06:30 and 18:29. The maximum tax amount per vehicle per day is 60&#160;SEK (6.53&#160;EUR, ).<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Payment is done by various means within 14 days after one has passed one of the control points; one cannot pay at the control points.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the trial period was over, consultative referendums were held in Stockholm Municipality and several other municipalities in Stockholm County. The then-reigning government (<a href="/wiki/Persson_Cabinet" title="Persson Cabinet">Persson Cabinet</a>) stated that they would only take into consideration the results of the referendum in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Municipality" title="Stockholm Municipality">Stockholm Municipality</a>. The opposition parties (<a href="/wiki/Alliance_(Sweden)" title="Alliance (Sweden)">Alliance for Sweden</a>) stated that if they were to form a cabinet after the <a href="/wiki/2006_Swedish_general_election" title="2006 Swedish general election">general election</a>\xe2\x80\x94which was held the same day as the congestion tax referendums\xe2\x80\x94they would take into consideration the referendums held in several of the other municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_County" title="Stockholm County">Stockholm County</a> as well. The results of the referendums were that the Stockholm Municipality voted for the congestion tax, while the other municipalities voted against it. The opposition parties won the general election and a few days before they formed government (<a href="/wiki/Reinfeldt_Cabinet" title="Reinfeldt Cabinet">Reinfeldt Cabinet</a>) they announced that the congestion tax would be reintroduced in Stockholm, but that the revenue would go entirely to road construction in and around Stockholm. During the trial period and according to the agenda of the previous government the revenue went entirely to public transport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">Ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg/220px-Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg/330px-Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg/440px-Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Viking_Grace_in_Stockholm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/MS_Viking_Grace" title="MS Viking Grace"><i>Viking Grace</i></a>, one of many <a href="/wiki/Cruiseferry" title="Cruiseferry">cruiseferries</a> on the routes to <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Islands" title="\xc3\x85land Islands">\xc3\x85land Islands</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Stockholm has regular ferry lines to <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turku" title="Turku">Turku</a> in Finland (commonly called "<a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea_cruiseferries" title="Baltic Sea cruiseferries">Finlandsf\xc3\xa4rjan</a>"); <a href="/wiki/Mariehamn" title="Mariehamn">Mariehamn</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Islands" title="\xc3\x85land Islands">\xc3\x85land</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>, Estonia; Riga, Latvia, and to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> in Russia. The large <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholm archipelago">Stockholm archipelago</a> is served by the archipelago boats of <a href="/wiki/Waxholmsbolaget" title="Waxholmsbolaget">Waxholmsbolaget</a> (owned and subsidized by Stockholm County Council).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_bikes">City bikes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: City bikes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Between April and October, during the warmer months, it is possible to rent <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Bikes" title="Stockholm City Bikes">Stockholm City Bikes</a> by purchasing a bike card online or through retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Cards allow users to rent bikes from any Stockholm City Bikes stand spread across the city and return them in any stand.<sup id="cite_ref-citybikes1_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citybikes1-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> There are two types of cards: the Season Card (valid from 1 April to 31 October) and the 3-day card. When their validity runs out they can be reactivated and are therefore reusable.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Bikes can be used for up to three hours per loan and can be rented from Monday to Sunday from 6 am to 10 pm.<sup id="cite_ref-citybikes1_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citybikes1-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/16px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></div><div class="pl"
