Airport">VST</a></b></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sweden_location_map,_40south.svg" title="File:Sweden location map, 40south.svg"> </a></div>Map showing the locations of airports around Stockholm</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>International and domestic:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport" title="Stockholm Arlanda Airport">Stockholm Arlanda Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>ARN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESSA</b>) is the largest and busiest airport in Sweden with 27&#160;million passengers in 2017. It is located about 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) north of Stockholm and serves as a hub for <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Bromma_Airport" title="Stockholm Bromma Airport">Stockholm Bromma Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>BMA</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESSB</b>) is located about 8&#160;km (5.0&#160;mi) west of Stockholm.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Only international:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Skavsta_Airport" title="Stockholm Skavsta Airport">Stockholm Skavsta Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>NYO</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESKN</b>) is located 108&#160;km (67&#160;mi) south of Stockholm. It is located 5&#160;km (3&#160;mi) away from <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6dermanland_County" title="S\xc3\xb6dermanland County">S\xc3\xb6dermanland County</a> capital <a href="/wiki/Nyk%C3%B6ping" title="Nyk\xc3\xb6ping">Nyk\xc3\xb6ping</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_V%C3%A4ster%C3%A5s_Airport" title="Stockholm V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s Airport">Stockholm V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>VST</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESOW</b>) is located 103&#160;km (64&#160;mi) west of Stockholm, in the city of <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4ster%C3%A5s" title="V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s">V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Express" title="Arlanda Express">Arlanda Express</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Airport_rail_link" title="Airport rail link">airport rail link</a> runs between <a href="/wiki/Arlanda_North_Station" title="Arlanda North Station">Arlanda Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a>. With a journey of 20 minutes, the train ride is the fastest way of traveling to the city center. <a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Central_Station" title="Arlanda Central Station">Arlanda Central Station</a> is also served by commuter, regional and intercity trains.\n</p><p>Additionally, there are also bus lines, <a href="/wiki/Flygbussarna" title="Flygbussarna">Flygbussarna</a>, that run between central Stockholm and all the airports.\n</p><p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there are no airports specifically for <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> in the Stockholm area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-city_trains">Inter-city trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Inter-city trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3442" data-file-height="1847" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm_centralstation_2017_-1_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a> has train connections to many Swedish cities as well as to <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Central_Station" title="Oslo Central Station">Oslo</a>, Norway and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Central_Station" title="Copenhagen Central Station">Copenhagen</a>, Denmark. The popular <a href="/wiki/X_2000" title="X 2000">X 2000</a> service to <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> takes three hours. Most of the trains are run by <a href="/wiki/SJ_AB" title="SJ AB">SJ AB</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_rankings">International rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: International rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Stockholm often performs well in international rankings, some of which are mentioned below:\n</p>\n<ul><li>In the book <i>The Ultimate Guide to International Marathons</i> (1997), written by Dennis Craythorn and Rich Hanna, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Marathon" title="Stockholm Marathon">Stockholm Marathon</a> is ranked as the best <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">marathon</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the 2006 <a href="/wiki/European_Innovation_Scoreboard" class="mw-redirect" title="European Innovation Scoreboard">European Innovation Scoreboard</a>, prepared by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Economic_Research_Institute_on_Innovation_and_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Maastricht Economic Research Institute on Innovation and Technology">Maastricht Economic Research Institute on Innovation and Technology</a> (MERIT) and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Research_Centre" title="Joint Research Centre">Joint Research Centre</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Protection_and_the_Security_of_the_Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute for the Protection and the Security of the Citizen">Institute for the Protection and the Security of the Citizen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, Stockholm was ranked as the most <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovative</a> city in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the 2008 World Knowledge Competitiveness Index, published by the Centre for International Competitiveness, Stockholm was ranked as the sixth most <a href="/wiki/Competition_(companies)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition (companies)">competitive</a> region in the world and the most competitive region outside the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the 2006 European Regional Growth Index (E-REGI), published by <a href="/wiki/JLL_(company)" title="JLL (company)">Jones Lang LaSalle</a>, Stockholm was ranked fifth on the list of European cities with the strongest <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> growth forecast. Stockholm was ranked first in Scandinavia and second outside Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the 2007 European Cities Monitor, published by <a href="/wiki/Cushman_%26_Wakefield" title="Cushman &amp; Wakefield">Cushman &amp; Wakefield</a>, Stockholm was ranked as the best Nordic city to locate a business. In the same report, Stockholm was ranked first in Europe in terms of freedom from <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In a 2007 survey performed by the environmental economist <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Kahn" title="Matthew Kahn">Matthew Kahn</a> for the <i><a href="/wiki/Reader%27s_Digest" title="Reader&#39;s Digest">Reader\'s Digest</a></i> magazine, Stockholm was ranked first on its list of the "greenest" and most "livable" cities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In a 2008 survey published by <i>Reader\'s Digest</i> magazine, Stockholm was ranked fourth in the world in its list of the "world\'s top ten honest cities".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In a 2008 survey published by the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Traveler" title="National Geographic Traveler">National Geographic Traveler</a></i> magazine, <a href="/wiki/Gamla_stan" title="Gamla stan">Gamla stan</a> (the old town) in Stockholm was ranked sixth on its list of rated historic places.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In a 2008 survey published by the <i><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy" title="Foreign Policy">Foreign Policy</a></i> magazine, Stockholm was ranked twenty-fourth on its list of the world\'s most global cities.<sup id="cite_ref-The_2008_Global_Cities_Index_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_2008_Global_Cities_Index-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In 2009 Stockholm was awarded the title as European Green Capital 2010, as the first Green capital ever in the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital_Award" title="European Green Capital Award">European Green Capital Award</a> scheme.</li>\n<li>In 2013, Stockholm was named the 8th most competitive city in the world by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In 2016 Stockholm was one of the cities with the most "unicorns" in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In 2019 Stockholm was awarded the World Smart City Award in the city category for its leadership of the European Smart Cities and Communities project GrowSmarter.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_cities_and_towns">Twin cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40"
